< Review>
They have a good variety of items here for amazing prices. I bought the entertainment center and 2 shelving units with cloth drawers here. They were very small, but, they work for what I need. The entertainment center feels as cheap as the $20 I paid for it, but the drawer systems felt surprisingly sturdy. All of the important pieces were in the box and mostly undamaged (some pieces were clearly scuffed and bumped, but I don't mind). All in all, the quality was slightly better than I expected, and it functions in the space exactly like I want it to. They also have storage tubs and buns and a small selection of groceries, household supplies, clothing, and electronics for great prices. Don't expect top shelf anything, but it'll all definitely get the job done.< /Review>

< Date>
1456520326728<//Date>
< rating>
3</rating>
< Text>
This location has everything you want from a Subway restaurant packed into a small space. It‚Äôs located in a strip mall at the intersection of two major streets. This makes it a popular destination and its popularity works against it when it‚Äôs busy. The restaurant has a dining room with six tables and an outdoor dining area with four tables. The outdoor dining area presses against Olive Avenue on one side and Victory Boulevard on the other and isn‚Äôt very pleasant. The soda tap is put into a nook between the door and where the line forms. Most of the day this place is pleasant and accessible. The staff here is wonderful with its owner in the kitchen and many long-time employees at the counter. During the Monday through Friday lunch rush I recommend ordering food online in advance and walking in to pick it up. At that time parking can be challenging. The line of people inside the restaurant will get long enough to co-mingle with people seated in the dining room. The soda tap becomes hard to access due to the line. The restaurant struggles at this time. The rest of the day and on weekends it‚Äôs just fine, though. This location accepts NFC payments.</Text>

Upon signing the contract I dropped down an initial payment in order to bring the financing of my system down (since I was purchasing my system and not leasing due to certain city restrictions). I was told that they would start submitting on my behalf all the paperwork to the city in order to get my rebate. Unfortunately we had missed the city's allocations for the Fiscal Year so we had to wait to the next FY to open up in order to submit for a rebate.

Give or take 4 months went by and I never heard back from Sunpro. Not an email to say we're working on your rebate with the city, or we're waiting on a certain date in order to submit your paperwork. I found myself making a lot of phone calls to my city's utilities company to find out what paperwork they needed and when was their deadlines. I was told several times by my city's utilities solar representative that I was doing a lot of the work that my contractor should have been doing. However if i had waited to hear back from Sunpro I would have missed my rebate allocation again.

I got on the phone and called Sunpro and spoke with someone at the sales desk. I asked if the contract was still on because I had been kept in the dark too long and I was honestly feeling like I had just lost a down payment on a system that was never going to happen. This was a several thousand dollar system and at this point I was not feeling any warm and fuzzies about this project. I seriously considered cancelling the project all together. Within an hour or so after the phone call I had Sam Strong on the line reassuring me that the installation was still on and that they were waiting on some things. However it would have been nice to be kept in the loop.

In short... I found myself doing a lot of the work that I thought should have been handled by Sunpro. I had to take time off work to make phone calls and ask about permits with the city such as PTO (permission to operate) and rebate information that I felt should have been provided by Sunpro. I would ask but no one seemed to give me a straight answer which is why I resorted to finding out for myself from the source.

In the end my system is working as designed and I am happy. However the road to the installation was a bit bumpy. Hopefully they have improved their customer service since last year 2013.</text><Pics>None</Pics><user>115191811964232332911< /user>< date>

<rate>4< /rate>< Review>
My experience with Sun Pro Solar is primarily positive, and my electric bills since having solar panels installed are at an all-time low (.49 cents was the most recent bill)!  Definitely a good decision overall.  The company and staff did a fine job for us and were very helpful and responsive to pour questions and concerns.
The only thing that prevents me from giving a five-star rating is that we had delays for the final inspections to pass because of various lack of communication issues between Sun Pro Solar and the city of Yorba Linda.  When dealing with this city, one should never assume that codes that pass in another city will pass in Yorba Linda.  I feel it was the solar company's responsibility to affirm with the city at the onset of the project all the specific codes that apply, and not assume that just because it passed in Buena Park or Newport Beach that it will pass in Yorba Linda.</Review>

Season 52 is a staple restaurant for celebration in my family. You would not expect the find a nice slice of decadence in a mall, but it's there with just the proper amount of class without the pomp and circumstance. They don't have a required dress code, but it's a respectable establish that people tend to actually look nice at.

Food quality is great. You could spend your entirety alone, dining on small plates and wine selection :-).

The staff is always courteous and have this far all been very educated on their menu selection. (Hats off the the chef and staff trainer).< /review>

<user_id>112503340733230276391<//user_id><name>Stefan Trinh</name><Date>1526086979740</Date><Rate>4< /Rate>< Review>
Came here for a early evening dinner at around 5:30pm. It was fairly busy. It was busier around the bar probably because of the happy hour drinks and food before 7pm on a weekday.

The place was nice, the atmosphere was also good and felt comfortable and welcome.

We had the spring three course meal:

Starter : potatoes and leek soup, asparagus soup
Mains: wood grilled fillet Mignon, wood grilled handline Tuna.
Desert: tiramisu, strawberry cheesecake.
Happy hour side: duck lollipops

3.5/5 -  The soups were good and tasty was ok, nice starter nothing too special But was very fresh.

4.5 / 5 -  The fillet mignon - it was tender and succulent. If it had a little more taste it would have been perfect but was still very tasty.

3.5/5 - The handline tuna - this looked terrific but the taste did not live up to the look. It was well plain and boring. Although you could taste that this was extremely fresh which is its saving grace.

5/5  -  Tiramisu a absolutely no complaints this is exactly how I like my Tiramisu. Flavoured rich but not to sweet. Perfecto.

4/5 - Strawberry cheesecake, good sweetness, wasn‚Äôt to my taste but could appreciate it is one of the better cheesecakes.

5/5 -  Duck legs, this is was probably the most exciting and best tasting dish we ate, plus it was a happy hour plate. Spicy flavourful, tender and fresh.

Service - 5/5 - we were serviced by Michelle, very nice and pleasant. Makes the experience much nicer. Thanks very much.

Overall I‚Äôm undecided it‚Äôs somewhere between 4 and 4.5. But one thing I will say about this place is if you want FRESH.

You get FRESH.

Thanks very much for the meal.</Review>

< text>
Came here for a early evening dinner at around 5:30pm. It was fairly busy. It was busier around the bar probably because of the happy hour drinks and food before 7pm on a weekday.

The place was nice, the atmosphere was also good and felt comfortable and welcome.

We had the spring three course meal:

Starter : potatoes and leek soup, asparagus soup
Mains: wood grilled fillet Mignon, wood grilled handline Tuna.
Desert: tiramisu, strawberry cheesecake.
Happy hour side: duck lollipops

3.5/5 -  The soups were good and tasty was ok, nice starter nothing too special But was very fresh.

4.5 / 5 -  The fillet mignon - it was tender and succulent. If it had a little more taste it would have been perfect but was still very tasty.

3.5/5 - The handline tuna - this looked terrific but the taste did not live up to the look. It was well plain and boring. Although you could taste that this was extremely fresh which is its saving grace.

5/5  -  Tiramisu a absolutely no complaints this is exactly how I like my Tiramisu. Flavoured rich but not to sweet. Perfecto.

4/5 - Strawberry cheesecake, good sweetness, wasn‚Äôt to my taste but could appreciate it is one of the better cheesecakes.

5/5 -  Duck legs, this is was probably the most exciting and best tasting dish we ate, plus it was a happy hour plate. Spicy flavourful, tender and fresh.

Service - 5/5 - we were serviced by Michelle, very nice and pleasant. Makes the experience much nicer. Thanks very much.

Overall I‚Äôm undecided it‚Äôs somewhere between 4 and 4.5. But one thing I will say about this place is if you want FRESH.

You get FRESH.

Thanks very much for the meal.< /text>

< Rate>
2< /Rate>
<review>The crabcake was pretty good. The use of spring mix seems dated in the small salad provided with the crabcake. The outside was crispy with the interior consisting of 90% crab meat, a pretty big plus for me. The entree I ordered, which was the bistro steak and potatoes, was not up to par.

First impressions were good, the plate was beautifully presented. On one side there were string beans and small white boiled potatoes. The potatoes were tossed, it seemed, in a herb butter. The other side of the plate consisted of what I'm guessing to be a 4oz sirloin blanked with the glistening red wine sauce detailed on the menu.

My first bite was the green beans. While I appreciate the fact they were not soggy wet, they were unfortunately not seasoned. NO SALT. I sought refuge in the potatoes hoping for an attempt at flavor, again a miss. The herb was parsley and again, no salt.

Hoping to salvage the meal I set my eyes on the steak. I sliced into my first piece of steak and dragged the bite through the red wine sauce. The sauce was flat and single note in flavor. It was just sour, and again lacking salt. And while I still can't figure out if the unpleasant bitter flavor I was experiencing was from the sauce or from the burnt steak. While the steak seemed to be quality, the quality was squandered from a lack of seasoning. I attempted to salvage my meal using table salt, unfortunately, the damage was already done. First impressions were good, the plate was beautifully presented. On one side there were string beans and small white boiled potatoes. The potatoes were tossed, it seemed, in a herb butter. <Review>Always a pleasure dining here.  As an Executive Chef, I find it hard to find great food and service that lives up to my own standards.  Every single time I dine here I am greeted genuinely, seated quickly, and served with connection by an engaged, cheerful and informative staff.
The food is as delightful as the service and I've yet to find a weak spot on the menu.  I can gladly say that in the four years I have been eating here, I haven't noticed one single flaw in the consistency of the entire experience.  That fact, in its own right, deserves the five star rating in today's marketplace.

My ONLY suggestion is the availability of fresh made desserts that don't come in a shot glass. Let your desserts be SO good people will come just for them!
My humble opinion as a faithful patron.

< text>
This was our second time dining at Seasons 52.  The first was 2 years ago and we really liked the food.  We were told by our waiter that the menu changed every week, hence the name.  This second visit was something of a disappointment.  The menu had not changed and one lady in our group had been back before and said it doesn't change.  Thursday nights aren't too busy and 5 of us were seated quickly, even without reservations.  Drink orders were quickly taken and water was served, then our orders, then we were forgotten.  My water glass had a big grease smear on the lip.  Finally, one of us got up and took it to the bartender.  He replaced it, and I swear, the second one had a big lip print.  My friend was embarrassed to return another glass, but we still couldn't get anyone's attention, and she was sitting on the outside of the booth.  Low points for service and cleanliness.  Then our food came.  My seared tuna salad failed to come with an extra dressing on the side, and when they brought it they also brought some dipping sauce for the tuna that was supposed to come with it.  It was OK, but not wonderful, with some odd pickled vegetables that were hard to identify.  The half chicken dinner was reported to taste good, but it was a little too colorless for my liking, it needed to be crisped under the broiler.  I was surprised that the two cooked entrees ordered were as small as they were.  No one went home with a box.  When you take all the above into account and add that there was no bread, soup or salad included, it comes to a rather outrageous price for a seared tuna salad and a glass of water, just about $21.50 plus a $4.00 tip.  I won't be returning.</text>

< Review>
I was skeptical, except that both Yelp & TripAdvisor almost universally positive.  We are too!

We went on a Tuesday at 5 PM.
Had the Happy Hour 2 glasses of wine -- one Happy Hour Chardonnay & one Happy Hour malbec -- & the chicken pesto flat bread, all for $15.  Both my wife & I -- both now about 70 years young -- loved it.  She then got the rainbow trout for $20, & I, the guy, got a Happy Hour spicy duck 'lollipop' & a Happy Hour lamb 'lollipop' -- & both, 3 of each, we're great!  Well recommended!  My better half loved her's too, & I did too, getting her sliced potatoes & several bites of her rainbow trout.  Plus, another glass of Happy Hour wine for each of us, Pinot gringio for her, & a Chilian Maipo Valley red blend for me, each $5.

Great atmosphere, & lots of happy people around us -- but not anything close to feel crowded, but just 'community'!

Great (lady) waitperson, too -- kudos to Taylor L!</Review>

<Rating>2<//Rating><gmap_id>0x809ada1e9621cce3:0xb645375b714abbb4< /gmap_id><Response>None</Response>< Text>
We had reservations for Valentine's day, and arrived 15 minutes early to check in. We were advised they were running 45 minutes behind and we ended up getting seated almost an hour past our reservation. This put a bit of a strain on other plans for the evening as well.

We had never been to Seasons 52 and heard great things.  Atmosphere was nice, ordered cocktails and both were not well mixed at all. Overheard people next to us complaining of raw chicken--prior to us ordering, which made us feel uneasy.
$14 for a hockey puck sized crab cake and I have had BETTER crab cakes.
I had filet mignon it was overcooked and not well seasoned. Yukon Gold mash was just that, mashed potatyo no added fats or seasoning. Broccolini was decent.
My other half had the roasted half chicken and had to request it had a crispier skin and make sure it is cooked through because of other patrons complaints.  Chicken came to the table nicely prepared, root vegetables were roasted but still under cooked almost raw and cold still.
Waiter came around with shot glass desserts that were underwhelming and overpriced, so we declined.
Service, outside of the delay was decent. Food I'll give 2/5 stars and no thumbs up.
My s.o says "there is a first and last for everything".. if we were to return again, it wo uld probably be another season and a new menu. But overall the check was definitely not worth the quality or quantity of food.</Text>

This place was absolutely obismal last night. Went there for the first time, with a friend who had been there multiple times and vouched for the place.

We were seated quickly, the environment was nice and the place was almost empty, so you would think service would be efficient and quick.....wrong!!

First, We ordered drinks, they arrived in a timley manner, but we had also ordered water with our drinks. The water never showed up, ther server came back and took our food order and said she would bring the water, aecond time she told us she wpuld bring our water, almost 30 minutes after we had already finished our appitizern the water finally showed up. In total probably 40 minutes just for water. But at least our nonwater beverages showed up in a reasonable time. We also tried to get her attention to add an order of veggies. But she was too preoccupied with her socialization and laughing with her coworkers over by the kitchen and that brings me to my second issue.

Second, I watched our server chit chat and socialize with the other servers more then I saw her attending her tables. Which is probably why our appetizer came out cold and why it took us which seemed forever to add an order of veggies.

Third, it took almost 30 minutes between our
appetizer (which is very small) being delivered and our main course to be delivered. And just before the main course, with our nonwater beverages empty, for quite some time, the water showed up and not ever 3 minutes later our main course showed up.

<Review>Let me preface this by saying I have worked as a waiter, bartender and bar manager for many years, and I am more than tolerant of things going wrong here and there.  However, this visit to Seasons 52 at the Arden Fair Mall was one of the worst dining experiences ever.  I could easily overlook one or two of the following incidents if they happened during the night, but there were way too many "incidents" lumped together for me to overlook.

1) The hostess led us to our both only to find out it was dirty.  She wiped off the table while my husband took a napkin and wiped off the dirty seats. 2) The waiter talked extremely fast and stayed at our table too long taking about what he liked and didn't like ("I'm from the South, so I really don't like tomatoes.  So if I give you one of these (makes a weird face), that means don't order that dish.").  3) The appetizer crab cake we ordered took a very long time to get to the table.  The waiter even admitted it was taking way too long.  When it came it was, well ehhh.  4) We ordered spinach salads, and a few minutes later we were told there was no more spinach.  We ordered different salads. 5) Shortly after our crab cake arrived, a runner brought us two spinach salads. I guess we looked shocked because the waiter said, "Well, this is the type of place that can run out of something one minute, but have it back the next.  I can see that spinach salad is back."  6) I asked for water then had to remind the waiter 10 minutes later when it did not come.  7) I ordered wine and had to to remind the waiter 15 minutes later when it didn't come.  8) Then the real waiting began.  We waited, and waited and waited for our entrees.  While I was in the restroom, the waiter came to tell us he was not sure what was taking so long.  9) We heard the manager apologizing or saying something to a group at the bar.  She offered to buy them drinks.  10) My husband called over the manager (because our waiter was absent more than he was seen).  We explained how poorly the evening had gone so far.  11) Ten minutes later she appeared with two plates saying, "I found them!"  I guess they must have been "lost".  12) My husband asked for his dessert to go.  But the waiter showed up with two ready to eat desserts and plopped them down on the table.  13) We both reminded him that we asked for the dessert TO GO.  We paid for the dinner with a $100 gift certificate, and the manager said she would comp the rest of the bill.  She also presented us with coupons for $100 worth of food and non-alcoholic beverages on our next visit.  Sorry dear, there will not be a next visit.
